Jamison Brereton

33 (267)
Visva╠Б ╠Дmitra and the Rivers
Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra G─Бthina / Rivers
13 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except anuс╣гс╣нubh 13
Although this hymn is found in the Indra collection, the Anukramaс╣З─л identifies Indra as the dedicand only of verses 6тАУ7, with the remainder divided between the rivers (Nadyas: 1тАУ3, 5, 9, 11тАУ13) and the poet himself, Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra (4, 8, 10). After two opening verses describing the confluence of the Vip─Б┼Ы and ┼Ъutudr─л rivers, this justly famous poem consists of a dialogue between those rivers and Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra, who begs the rivers to stop in their course to allow the Bharata forces, under his patron, King Sud─Бs (not named here, but see III.53.9), to cross. They accede to his request in return for his ensuring their future fame in his poetry, and the Bharatas cross successfully, as is announced in verse 12тАФafter which the rivers are urged to refill themselves with water and flow again. That it is the poet who succeeds in temporarily stopping the rivers is yet another example of the power of properly formulated speech to control the physical world. The final verse (13), in a different meter, may be a magic spell, exemplifying the continuing belief in the power of the word by applying this legendary river crossing to a team in trouble at a ford.514 III.33

Jamison Brereton Notes

English translation:

тАЬRushing from the flanks of the mountains, eager (to reach the sea) like two mares with loosened reins contending (with each other in speed), like two fair mother cows (hastening) to caress (their calves), the Vip─Бs’ and ┼Ъutudri, flow readily with (united) waterс╣гтАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

┼Ъutudri: legend (also given in Nirukta 2.24): Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra, the family priest of Sud─Бs, the son of Paijavana, having gained much wealth in his service, was returning with it home, when his road brought him to the confluence of the Vip─Бs’ and ┼Ъutudri; in order to make them fordable, he addressed to them the first verses of this s┼лkta, to which he replied, and allowed him and his followers to cross

Jamison Brereton

Forth from the lap of the mountains, eager, racing with each other like two mares unloosed,
resplendent, licking each other like mother cows (their calves), the Vip─Б┼Ы and ┼Ъutudr─л (rivers) speed with their milk.

Griffith

FORTH from the bosom of the mountains, eager as two swift mares with loosened rein contending,
Like two bright mother cows who lick their youngling, Vipas and Sutudri speed down their waters.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬImpelled by Indra, soliciting (his commands), you go to the ocean like charioteers (to their goal); flowing together, and swelling with (your) waves, bright (rivers) one of you proceeds to the other.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Impelled by Indra as you long to take part in the forward thrust, you drive like two charioteers to the sea,
clashing together, swelling with your waves, the one of you merges into the otherтАФyou resplendent ones.

Jamison Brereton Notes

├нndreс╣гite echoes v├нс╣гite in 1b, though they belong to two different roots: тИЪiс╣г тАШimpelтАЩ and тИЪs─Б тАШtieтАЩ respectively. The basis for calling the rivers ├нndreс╣гite is given in 6ab.

Although by my rule (тАЬVedic any├б- тАШanother, the other’ тАжтАЭ; Fs. Beekes 1997, 111-18), forms of any├б- found initial in the p─Бda should be indefinite (тАШanotherтАЩ) not definite as here, the any├│тАШnyam (тАЬthe one тАж the otherтАЭ) construction works differently.

Griffith

Impelled by Indra whom ye pray to urge you, ye move as ’twere on chariots to the ocean.
Flowing together, swelling with your billows, O lucid Streams, each of you seeks the other.

Geldner

Von Indra angetrieben, um das Zeichen zum Galopp bittend, geht ihr wie zwei Wagenrosse. Wenn ihr mit den Wogen anschwellend euch vereinigt habt, geht die eine von euch in der anderen auf, ihr Schmucken.

Erregt von Indra, schnelle Str├╢mung heischend, wie Wagenlenker eilet ihr zum Meere; Zusammenrinnend und von Wogen schwellend, so lauft ihr Sch├╢nen nahe beieinander.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI repaired to the most material river; I went to the wide auspicious Vip─Бs’, flowing together to a common receptacle, like parent cows (hastening to) caress the calf.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

[Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra:] I have driven to the most motherly river [=┼Ъutudr─л]; we have come to the broad, well-portioned Vip─Б┼ЫтАФ
the two who are like mothers together licking their calf, proceeding together along the same womb [=riverbed].

Griffith

I have attained the most maternal River, we have approached Vipas, the broad, the blessed.
Licking as ’twere their calf the pair of Mothers flow onward to their common home together.

Geldner

Ich bin zu dem m├╝tterlichsten Strom gekommen, wir sind an die breite holde Vipas gelangt, die sich beide lecken wie Mutterk├╝he ein Kalb, indem sie im gemeinsamen Bette weiterlaufen.

Grassmann

Ich fuhr herbei zum m├╝tterlichsten Strome, wir kamen zur Vip─Б├з, der breiten, sch├╢nen, Zum M├╝tterpaar, das, wie sein Kalb beleckend, zu gleichem Schoosse hin zusammen wandert.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe rivers speak: Fertilizing (the land) with this (our) current, we are flowing to the receptacle which has been appointed by the deity (Indra); the course appointed for our going (permits) not of delay; of what is the sage desirious, that he addresses the rivers?тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

[Rivers:] So we areтАФswelling with milk, proceeding along our god-made womb.
Our forward thrust, launched in a surge, is not to be obstructed. Seeking what does the poet keep calling upon the rivers?

Jamison Brereton Notes

The reference of the rivers switches from dual to plural here and remains so (save for two singulars in 10cd). There is no obvious reason for this change, though it may reflect the fact that when the two rivers merge into each other they form a third.

Griffith

We two who rise and swell with billowy waters move forward to the home which Gods have made us.
Our flood may not be stayed when urged to motion. What would the singer, calling to the Rivers?

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬVi┼Ыv─Бmitra speaks: Rivers, charged with water, rest a moment from your course at my request, who go to gather the Soma; I, the son of Ku┼Ыika, desirous of protection, address with earnest prayer especially the river before me.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

At my request: me vacase somy─Бya = to my speech importing the soma, i.e. the object of my address is, that having crossed over, I may go to gather the soma; cf. Nirukta 2.25; the river before me: that is, the ┼Ыutudri

Jamison Brereton

[Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra:] Stop for my somian speech, truthful ones, for an instant, in your travels.
My lofty inspired thought (has gone) forth to the river: seeking help, have I, the son of Ku┼Ыika, called upon (you).

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner renders voc. с╣Ы╠Бt─Бvar─лс╕е as тАШihr ImmerfliessendenтАЩ without comment. But this is simply the fem. stem to the possessive с╣Ыt─Б╠Бvan- тАШpossessing с╣Ыt├б-тАЩ, which he elsewhere tr. тАЬgesetzestreuenтАЭ (e.g., I.160.1, III.54.4) et sim.

In 5c avasy├║- тАШseeking helpтАЩ answers the question posed by the rivers in 4c kiс╣Гy├║- тАШseeking what?тАЩ and in the same position in the vs. _________ 06
In this vs. the rivers indirectly respond to Vi┼Ыv─БmitraтАЩs command тАЬStop!тАЭ (r├бmadhvam) in the previous vs. (5a), by asserting that they flow because of the efforts of and at the pleasure of the gods: Indra dug their channels and, by smashing Vс╣Ыtra, removed the barrier to their movement; Savitar led them and they flow at his impulsion. Without explicitly refusing Vi┼Ыv─БmitraтАЩs request, they make it plain that they wonтАЩt comply by stopping.

The stem prasav├б- тАШforward thrust, impulsionтАЩ occurs here for the third time in this hymn (2a, 4c, 6d; see also 11c) and is here associated with its etymological divinity Savitar, the Impeller.

Griffith

Linger a little at my friendly bidding rest, Holy Ones, a moment in your journey.
With hymn sublime soliciting your favour Kusika’s son hath called unto the River.

Geldner

Haltet meiner somagleichen Rede auf einen Augenblick in eurem Laufe still, ihr Immerflie├Яenden! An den Flu├Я ergeht ein hohes Ansinnen. Schutzsuchend habe ich, des Kusika Sohn, gerufen.

Grassmann

Erg├╢tzet euch an meinem frommen Liede auf kurze Rast in eurem Lauf, o heil’ge; Zum Strome dringt des Herzens laute Bitte, verlangend rief ich euch, der Sohn des Ku├зik.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe rivers speak; Indra, the wielder of the thunder-bolt, dug our channels when he slew Ahi the blocker-up of rivers; the divine and well-handed Savit─Б has led us (on our path), and obedient tohis commands we flow (as) ample (streams).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The blocker-yo if ruversL tge ckiyd unorusibubg the water of the rains;

Savit─Б: epithet of Indra, the impeller or animator of the world: savit─Б sarvasya jagataс╕е prerakaс╕е; cf. Nirukta 2.26

Jamison Brereton

[Rivers:] Indra with the mace in his arms dug us channels: he smashed away Vr╠еtra [/the obstacle] surrounding the rivers.
God Savitar of the lovely hands led (us): at his forward thrust we journey widely.

Griffith

Indra who wields the thunder dug our channels: he smote down Vrtra, him who stayed our currents.
Savitar, God, the lovely-handed, led us, and at his sending forth we flow expanded.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рднреВрдорд┐ рдЖрджрд┐ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдереЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЖрдХрд░реНрд╖рдг рд╕реЗ рдпрдерд╛рд╕реНрдерд╛рди рдард╣рд░рд╛ рдФрд░ рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐ рдХрд░рдХреЗ рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдп рдХреЛ рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрди рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╣реА рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧ рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рдЖрдХрд░реНрд╖рдг рдФрд░ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдУрдВ рдХреЛ рдЬреАрдд рдХрд░рдХреЗ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдп рдХреА рд╢реЛрднрд╛ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░реЗрдВ рееремрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрдиреНрдирд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рдпрдерд╛ рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рджреЗрд╡реЛ рдирджреАрдирд╛рдВ рдкрд░рд┐рдзрд┐рдВ рд╡реГрддреНрд░рдордкрд╛рд╣рдиреН рддрджрд╡рдпрд╡рд╛рдирд░рджрдЬреНрдЬрд▓рдВ рднреВрдорд┐рдВ рдЪрд╛рдирдпрддреНрддрдерд╛ рд╡рдЬреНрд░рдмрд╛рд╣реБрдГ рд╕рдиреНрдирд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рд╕рдВрд░рдХреНрд╖реНрдп рд╕рд╕реЗрд╡рдХрд╛рдВрд╢реНрдЫрддреНрд░реВрдиреН рд╣рдиреНрдпрд╛рддреН рдпрдГ рд╕реБрдкрд╛рдгрд┐рд░реНрджреЗрд╡рд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдореБрд░реНрд╡реА рд░рдХреНрд╖реЗрд╕реНрддрд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рд╕рд╡реЗ рд╡рдпрдорд╛рдирдиреНрджрдВ рдпрд╛рдордГ рееремрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрде рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддреЗрди рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╡реНрдпрдорд╛рд╣ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬVi┼Ыv─Бmitra speaks: Ever is that heroic exploit of Indra to be celebrated when he cut Ahi to pieces, and with his thunderbolt destroyed the surrounding (obstructors of the rain), whence the waters proceed in the direction they desire.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

[Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra:] This act of heroism is to be proclaimed ever anew, the deed of Indra when he hewed apart the serpent.
He smashed apart the enclosures with his mace. The waters went seeking a way to go.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This is the central vs. of the hymn; in it Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra practices the kind of praise poetry that the rivers will ask him to reproduce in perpetuity in vs. 8, couched in high formal style. In fact it can be seen as a variant of the opening of the great Indra hymn I.32.1: ├нndrasya n├║ v─лry─Б╠Ас╣Зi pr├б vocaс╣Г, y─Б╠Бni cak─Б╠Бra тАж Here we have the gerundive prav─Б╠Бcyam for pr├б vocam, v─лry├аm matching v─лry─Б╠Ас╣Зi, ├нndrasya as in I.32, and the nominalization k├бrma for the pf. cak─Б╠Бra. The serpent, the mace, and the signature verb тИЪhan are then found in the rest of b and in c, as they are in I.32.1. As Watkins points out (Dragon, 309), here the verb тИЪhan has been displaced from its standard formulaic role, with ├бhim as object, to an adjacent part of the myth. Watkins also points out (86 n. 2) that there is тАЬa veritable constellation of inherited words and roots relating to poetry in this passageтАЭ (apropos vss. 7-8).

Note the etymological and phonetic figure ─Б╠Бyan тАж ├бyanam in d.

Griffith

That hero deed of Indra must be lauded for ever that he rent Ahi in pieces.
He smote away the obstructors with his thunder, and eager for their course forth flowed the waters.

Dies Heldenwerk ist immerdar zu preisen, das Indra that, als er zerhieb die Schlange; Mit seinem Blitze schlug er die Umlagrer, die Wasser gingen, die den Gang begehrten.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe rivers speak: Praiser of Indra, forget not this speech, nor the worlds that (you have addressed to us) for future ages (to reverence); celebrator (of holy rites), be favourable to us in solemn prayers; treat us not after the (arrogant fashion) of men; salutation be to you!тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

[Rivers:] This speech, singerтАФdo not forget itтАФso that later generations will hear it from you.
Favor us in return in your hymns, bard: donтАЩt put us down among men. Homage to you.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Though med. juс╣г├бte overwhelmingly means тАШenjoyтАЩ, the addition of the preverb pr├бti sometimes yields a transitive тАШfavor in return, in responseтАЩ with personal obj. See disc. ad IX.92.1.

Griffith

Never forget this word of thine, O singer, which future generations shall reecho.
In hymns, O bard, show us thy loving kindness. Humble us not mid men. To thee be honour!

Geldner

Dieses Wort solltest du, o S├дnger, nicht vergessen, das k├╝nftige Geschlechter von dir h├╢ren m├╢gen. Sei uns, o Dichter, in deinen Liedern gef├дllig, setz uns nicht bei den Menschen herab! Ehre sei dir!

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬVi┼Ыv─Бmitra speaks: Listen, sister (streams), kindly to him who praises you; who has come from afar with a waggon and chariot; bow down lowly; become easily fordable; remain, rivers, lower than the axle (of the wheel) with your currents.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

With a wagon and chariot: anas─Б rathena = ┼Ыakaс╣нena rathena ca, by a cart and a carriage; anas, a cart or wagon, or truck, to convey the Soma

Jamison Brereton

[Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra:] Listen well to the bard, sisters. He has driven to you from afar with his wagon and chariot.
Bow down; become easy to cross, staying below his axle(s) with your currents, you rivers.

Griffith

List quickly, Sisters, to the bard who cometh to you from far away with car and wagon.
Bow lowly down; be easy to be traversed stay, Rivers, with your floods below our axles.

Geldner

Schenket doch, ihr Schwestern, dem Dichter Geh├╢r! Er ist mit Wagentro├Я und Streitwagen zu euch aus der Ferne gekommen. Beuget euch fein nieder, seid leicht zu durchschreiten, bleibet mit eurer Str├╢mung unter den Wagenachsen, ihr Fl├╝sse!

Grassmann

So h├╢rt denn recht, o Schwestern, auf den Dichter; ich naht’ von fern euch mit beladnem Wagen; Neigt nieder euch, seid leicht mir zu durchfahren, nicht flutend bis zur Achse, o ihr Str├╢me.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe rivers speak: Hymner, we hear your words, that you have come from afar with a wagon and chariot; we bow down before you; like a woman nursing (her child), like a maiden bending to embrace a man, (so will we do) for you.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

For you: te is repeated at the end of the line; it is repeated out of respect, te iti punaruktir ─Бdar─Бrtham

Jamison Brereton

[Rivers:] We will listen to your words, bard. You have driven from afar with wagon and chariot.
I [=one river] will bow down to you like a young woman swollen (with milk, to her infant), (while) I [=other river] will bend to you like a maiden to her cavalier.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although the two rivers refer to themselves collectively in the 1st pl. in ab, the second hemistich consists of two contrasting statements in the 1st sg., each presumably made by one of the rivers. This balanced contrast accounts for the accent on the 2nd verb ┼Ыa┼Ыvaca├н.

Griffith

Yea, we will listen to thy words, O singer. With wain and car from far away thou comest.
Low, like a nursing mother, will I bend me, and yield me as a maiden to her lover.

Geldner

Wir wollen deinen Worten Geh├╢r schenken, o Dichter. Du bist mit Wagentro├Я und Streitwagen aus der Ferne gekommen. Ich will mich dir neigen wie die milchgeschwellte Frau zu ihrem Kinde, w├дhrend ich dir nachgeben will, wie das M├дdchen ihrem Liebsten.

Grassmann

┬╗Wir wollen achten deiner Wort’, o Dichter, du kamst von ferne mit beladnem Wagen; Dir neig’ ich mich wie eine ├╝pp’ge Buhle, wie ihrem Mann die Braut ergeb’ ich dir mich.┬л

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬVi┼Ыv─Бmitra speaks: (Since), rivers, (you have allowed me to cross), so may the Bharatas pass over (your united stream); may the troop desiring to cross the water, permitted (by you), and impelled by Indra, pass; then let the course appinted for your going (be resumed); I have recourse to the favour of you who are worthy of adoration.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The Bharatas: said to be the same lineage as Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra’s: bharakulaj─Б madiy─Бс╕е sarve; perhaps this means, those who were the bearers of Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra’s goods and chattels; Mah─Бbh─Бrata, ─Аdi Parva 5.3734 cites Vasiс╣гс╣нha as the family priest of the Bharatas

Jamison Brereton

[Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra:] When the Bharatas should really have crossed you entirelyтАФthe horde seeking cattle, propelled, sped by IndraтАФ then certainly your forward thrust, launched in a surge, will rush
(again). I wish for the favor of you who deserve the sacrifice.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As in the immediately preceding hymn III.32.9-10, the poet here seems to be trying to express verbal nuances that are not coded systematically in the Vedic verbal system, in particular another variety of anteriority. Here the sequence of moods is unusual: pres. optative in the subord. cl. (saс╣Гt├бreyuс╕е), pres. subjunctive in the main cl. (├бrс╣г─Бt). With the optative he seems to be aiming at a future perfect (тАЬwill/would have crossedтАЭ) whose prospective action precedes that of the main verb, namely the subjunctive referring to future time. Although I have not examined the entire RV with this in mind, these experiments in anteriority seem confined to – or at least especially pronounced in – the work of this poet. Note also that the poet makes no attempt to generate an opt. to the pf. tat─Бra or to use the already existing pf. opt.

tutury─Б╠Б- (RV 5x). This provides further evidence, if more were needed, against DahlтАЩs claim that the pf. opt. denotes тАЬepistemic possibility and anterior aspectтАЭ (Time, Tense and Aspect, p. 402 and in general pp. 392-402). If this were a stable function of the pf. opt., surely Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra would have availed himself of that formation.

The vs. reprises much of the vocabulary from earlier in the hymn: iс╣гit├б ├нndraj┼лtaс╕е is an elaboration on ├нndreс╣гita- in 2a; the oft-repeated prasav├б- returns again in the expression prasav├бс╕е s├бrgataktaс╕е repeated from 4c.

Griffith

Soon as the Bharatas have fared across thee, the warrior band, urged on and sped by Indra,
Then let your streams flow on in rapid motion. I crave your favour who deserve our worship.

Geldner

Wenn die Bharata┬┤s dich wirklich ├╝berschritten haben werden, der auf Rinderbeute ausziehende Heerbann, zur Eile getrieben, von Indra angefeuert, dann soll euer Galopp pfeilschnell dahinschie├Яen. Die Gunst erbitte ich von euch, den Verehrungsw├╝rdigen.

Grassmann

Wenn nun das Heer der Bharater voll Kampflust beeilt von Indra schnell dich hat durchschritten, Dann schiesse vor die pfeilgeschwinde Str├╢mung, um diese Gnade fleh’ ich euch, ihr hehren.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬThe Bharat─Бs seeking cattle passed over; the sage enjoyed the favour of the rivers; streams dispensing food, productive of wealth, spread abundance, fill (your beds), flow swiftly.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

[Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra:] The cattle-seeking Bharatas have entirely crossed; the poet has shared in the favor of the rivers.
Swell forth, nurturing, very generous; fill your bellies; drive quickly.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The prospective action expressed by the opt. saс╣Гt├бreyuс╕е in 11a is announced as completed by the aor. ├бt─Бriс╣гuс╕е тАж s├бm тАШthey have crossedтАЩ, and the poet urges the rivers to flow again with a sequence of imperatives, elaborating on the subj. ├бrс╣г─Бt in 11c.

Griffith

The warrior host, the Bharatas, fared over the singer won the favour of the Rivers.
Swell with your billows, hasting, pouring riches. Fill full your channels, and roll swiftly onward.

рдЗрддреНрдпрдбрднрд╛рд╡рдГ ред рдирд┐рдШрд╛рддрдГ рее реерезрекрее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet your waves (rivers) so flow that the pin of the yoke may be above (their) waters; leave the traces full, and may (the two streams), exempt from misfortune or defect, and uncensured, exhibit no (present) increase.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The pin: ┼Ыamy─Б, yugk─лla; or, the ropes that are fastened to the ends of the yoke, the traces: yugyakaс╣Зс╣нha p─Бr┼Ыv─Бdi saс╣Гlagna rajjavaс╕е; yoktr─Бс╣Зi is also similarly explained; perhaps, these refer to the traces; exhibit no present increase: ma ┼Ы┼лnam ─Бrat─Бm: ┼Ы┼лnam = samс╣Ыddhim, increase, referring merely to the present moment; i.e., may the rivers not so rise as to prevent his passage; or, it may convey a wish that the rivers might never suffer any diminution, taking ┼Ы┼лnam in the sense of ┼Ы┼лnyam, emptiness

Jamison Brereton

Let your wave push up the yoke-pins; o waters, let loose the
yoking cords.
Let the two inviolable (oxen), doing no ill, without offense, not come to naught.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Hoffmann (Injunk, 93 n. 184) thinks the first impv. is concessive: тАЬMag eure Welle an die ┼Ыamy─Бs schlagen, die Geschirre lasst freiтАЭ – this may well be, but a little hard to tell given our lack of teamster texts.

Griffith

So let your wave bear up the pins, and ye, O Waters, spare the thongs;
And never may the pair of Bulls, harmless and sinless, waste away.

Geldner

Eure Welle soll die Jochzapfen emporheben, ihr Gew├дsser, gebet die Str├дnge frei! Nicht sollen die schuldlosen Rinder, die nichts ├Ьbles tun, in Verlust geraten!

Grassmann

Die Zapfen schlag’ die Well’ empor, o Wasser l├╢st die B├дnder ab, nicht sch├дdigt das unschuldige, das fehlerlose Stierepaar.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рдпреЛ рднрд╡рдиреНрддреНрдпрдГ рд╢рдореНрдпрд╛ рдЖрдк рдЗрд╡ рджреБрдГрдЦрдВ рд╣рдиреНрддреБ рдпреЛ рд╡ рдКрд░реНрдорд┐рд░рд┐рд╡реЛрддреНрд╕рд╛рд╣реЗрди рдпреЛрдХреНрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рдпреВрдпрдВ рдореБрдЮреНрдЪрддред рд╣реЗ рд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрдкреБрд░реБрд╖реМ рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдорджреБрд╖реНрдХреГрддреМ рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрдВ рдорд╛рд░рддрд╛рдВ рд╡реНрдпреЗрдирд╕рд╛рдШреНрдиреНрдпреМ рд╕рддреНрдпреМ рдкрддрд┐рдГ рдкрддреНрдиреА рдЪ рджреНрд╡реМ рд╢реВрдирдВ рд╕реБрдЦрдореБрджрд╛рд░рддрд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрддрд╛рдореН реерезрейрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ред

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЙрддреН) рдЙрддреНрдХреГрд╖реНрдЯреЗ (рд╡рдГ) рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдиреН (рдКрд░реНрдорд┐рдГ) рддрд░рдЩреНрдЧ рдЗрд╡реЛрддреНрд╕рд╛рд╣рдГ (рд╢рдореНрдпрд╛рдГ) рд╢рдореНрдпрд╛рдВ рдХрд░реНрдордгрд┐ рднрд╡рд╛рдГ (рд╣рдиреНрддреБ) рджреВрд░реАрдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддреБ (рдЖрдкрдГ) рдЬрд▓рд╛рдиреАрд╡ (рдпреЛрдХреНрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐) рдпреЛрдЬрдирд╛рдирд┐ (рдореБрдЮреНрдЪрдд) рддреНрдпрдЬрдд (рдорд╛) рдирд┐рд╖реЗрдзреЗ (рдЕрджреБрд╖реНрдХреГрддреМ) рдЕрджреБрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░рд┐рдгреМ (рд╡реНрдпреЗрдирд╕рд╛) рд╡рд┐рдирд╖реНрдЯрдкрд╛рдкрд╛рдЪрд░рдгреЗрди (рдЕрдШреНрдиреНрдпреМ) рд╣рдиреНрддреБрдордирд░реНрд╣реЗ (рд╢реВрдирдореН) рд╕реБрдЦрдореНред рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдордкреАрддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред (рдЖ) (рдЕрд░рддрд╛рдореН) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрддрд╛рдореН реерезрейрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпреМ рд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрдкреБрд░реБрд╖реМ рджреБрдГрдЦрдмрдиреНрдзрдирд╛рдирд┐рдЪреНрдЫрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░рдВ рд╡рд┐рд╣рд╛рдп рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреЛрдиреНрдирддрд┐рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛рддрд╛рдВ рддреМ рд╕рддрддрдВ рд╕реБрдЦрдорд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдпрд╛рддрд╛рдорд┐рддрд┐ реерезрейрее рдЕрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдШрдирджреАрд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рддреНрд╕рдЦрд┐рд╢рд┐рд▓реНрдкрд┐рдиреМрдХрд╛рджрд┐рд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрдкреБрд░реБрд╖рдХреГрддреНрдпрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рддреНрд░рдпрд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрджрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГрее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЗ рд╕реНрддреНрд░реА-рдкреБрд░реБрд╖ рджреБрдГрдЦрдмрдВрдзрдирд╛рддреВрди рд╕реБрдЯрддрд╛рдд рд╡ рджреБрд╖реНрдЯ рдЖрдЪрд░рдгрд╛рдЪрд╛ рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧ рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд рдЖрдгрд┐ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреЗрдЪреА рд╡реГрджреНрдзреА рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд рддреЗ рдирд┐рд░рдВрддрд░ рд╕реБрдЦ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд. рее резрей рее
